	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Caitlyn Jenner</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bruce_Jenner&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Bruce Jenner">Bruce Jenner</a>)</span></div>

</div></div></th></tr><tr><td colspan="2"></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Website</th><td><span class="official-website"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://caitlynjenner.com/">Official website</a></span></span> <a href="https://www.wikidata.org/wiki/Q365144#P856" title="Edit this at Wikidata"><img alt="Edit this at Wikidata" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Blue_pencil.svg/10px-Blue_pencil.svg.png" decoding="async" width="10" height="10" style="vertical-align: text-top" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Blue_pencil.svg/15px-Blue_pencil.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Blue_pencil.svg/20px-Blue_pencil.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600" /></a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Caitlyn Marie Jenner</b> (born <b>William Bruce Jenner</b>; October 28, 1949) is an American <a href="/wiki/Television_personality" class="mw-redirect" title="Television personality">television personality</a> and retired <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic</a> <a href="/wiki/Olympic_medal" title="Olympic medal">gold medal</a>–winning <a href="/wiki/Decathlon" title="Decathlon">decathlete</a>.
</p><p>Jenner played <a href="/wiki/College_football" title="College football">college football</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Graceland_Yellowjackets" title="Graceland Yellowjackets">Graceland Yellowjackets</a> before incurring a knee injury that required surgery. Convinced by Olympic decathlete <a href="/wiki/Jack_Parker_(decathlete)" title="Jack Parker (decathlete)">Jack Parker</a>'s coach, <a href="/wiki/L._D._Weldon" title="L. D. Weldon">L.&#160;D.&#160;Weldon</a>, to try the <a href="/wiki/Decathlon" title="Decathlon">decathlon</a>, Jenner won the <a href="/wiki/Athletics_at_the_1976_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_decathlon" title="Athletics at the 1976 Summer Olympics – Men&#39;s decathlon">men's decathlon</a> event at the <a href="/wiki/1976_Summer_Olympics" title="1976 Summer Olympics">1976 Summer Olympics in Montreal</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-KindelanEffron_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KindelanEffron-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-giardina_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-giardina-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> setting a third successive world record and gaining fame as "an all-American hero".<sup id="cite_ref-dmr_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dmr-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Given the unofficial title of "world's greatest athlete",<sup id="cite_ref-world&#39;s_greatest_athlete_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-world&#39;s_greatest_athlete-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Jenner established a career in television, film, writing, auto racing, business, and as a <i><a href="/wiki/Playgirl" title="Playgirl">Playgirl</a></i> cover model.<sup id="cite_ref-formerly_bruce_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-formerly_bruce-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Jenner has six children with three successive wives—Chrystie Crownover, <a href="/wiki/Linda_Thompson_(actress)" title="Linda Thompson (actress)">Linda Thompson</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kris_Jenner" title="Kris Jenner">Kris Jenner</a>—and has since 2007 appeared on the <a href="/wiki/Reality_television" title="Reality television">reality television</a> series <i><a href="/wiki/Keeping_Up_with_the_Kardashians" title="Keeping Up with the Kardashians">Keeping Up with the Kardashians</a></i> with Kris, their daughters <a href="/wiki/Kendall_Jenner" title="Kendall Jenner">Kendall</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kylie_Jenner" title="Kylie Jenner">Kylie Jenner</a>, and Kris's other children <a href="/wiki/Kourtney_Kardashian" title="Kourtney Kardashian">Kourtney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kim_Kardashian" title="Kim Kardashian">Kim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khlo%C3%A9_Kardashian" title="Khloé Kardashian">Khloé</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rob_Kardashian" title="Rob Kardashian">Rob Kardashian</a>. <a href="/wiki/Sex_assignment" title="Sex assignment">Assigned</a> male at birth, Caitlyn Jenner publicly <a href="/wiki/Coming_out" title="Coming out">came out</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Trans_woman" title="Trans woman">trans woman</a> in April 2015. Her new name was publicly announced in July of that year, with her name and gender being legally changed the following September.<sup id="cite_ref-legal_name_change_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-legal_name_change-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> From 2015 to 2016, Jenner starred in the reality television series <i><a href="/wiki/I_Am_Cait" title="I Am Cait">I Am Cait</a></i>, which focused on her <a href="/wiki/Gender_transition" class="mw-redirect" title="Gender transition">gender transition</a>. In January 2017, she underwent <a href="/wiki/Sex_reassignment_surgery_(male-to-female)" title="Sex reassignment surgery (male-to-female)">sex reassignment surgery</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Jenner has been called the most famous <a href="/wiki/Transgender" title="Transgender">transgender</a> woman in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Pilkington_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pilkington-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Transgender_reality_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Transgender_reality-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>
<p>Caitlyn Marie Jenner was born William Bruce Jenner on October 28, 1949, in <a href="/wiki/Mount_Kisco,_New_York" title="Mount Kisco, New York">Mount Kisco, New York</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-born_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-born-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> to Esther Ruth (<i>née</i> McGuire) and William Hugh Jenner. Her father was an <a href="/wiki/Arborist" title="Arborist">arborist</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-geni_bio_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geni_bio-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Crownover_1986_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crownover_1986-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> She is of English, Scottish, Irish, Dutch, and Welsh descent.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Her younger brother, Burt, was killed in a car accident in <a href="/wiki/Canton,_Connecticut" title="Canton, Connecticut">Canton, Connecticut</a> on November 30, 1976, shortly after Jenner's success at the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic Games</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-scinto_crash_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scinto_crash-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-People_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-People-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> As a young child, Jenner was diagnosed with <a href="/wiki/Dyslexia" title="Dyslexia">dyslexia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cooper_gold_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cooper_gold-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Jenner attended Sleepy Hollow High School in <a href="/wiki/Sleepy_Hollow,_New_York" title="Sleepy Hollow, New York">Sleepy Hollow, New York</a>, for her freshman and <a href="/wiki/Sophomore" title="Sophomore">sophomore</a> years<sup id="cite_ref-school_pals_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-school_pals-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-return_to_tarrytown_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-return_to_tarrytown-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Newtown_High_School_(Connecticut)" title="Newtown High School (Connecticut)">Newtown High School</a> in <a href="/wiki/Newtown,_Connecticut" title="Newtown, Connecticut">Newtown, Connecticut</a>, for her junior and senior years, graduating in 1968.<sup id="cite_ref-name_taken_off_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-name_taken_off-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Jenner earned a <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">football</a> <a href="/wiki/Scholarship" title="Scholarship">scholarship</a> and attended Graceland College (now <a href="/wiki/Graceland_University" title="Graceland University">Graceland University</a>) in <a href="/wiki/Lamoni,_Iowa" title="Lamoni, Iowa">Lamoni, Iowa</a>, but was forced to stop playing football because of a knee injury.<sup id="cite_ref-HolstPopp2004_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HolstPopp2004-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Recognizing Jenner's potential, Graceland track coach <a href="/wiki/L._D._Weldon" title="L. D. Weldon">L. D. Weldon</a> encouraged Jenner to switch to the <a href="/wiki/Decathlon" title="Decathlon">decathlon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-champion_within_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-champion_within-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Jenner debuted as a decathlete in 1970 in the <a href="/wiki/Drake_Relays" title="Drake Relays">Drake Relays</a> decathlon in <a href="/wiki/Des_Moines,_Iowa" title="Des Moines, Iowa">Des Moines, Iowa</a>, finishing in fifth place.<sup id="cite_ref-history_of_icons_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history_of_icons-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Jenner graduated from Graceland College in 1973 with a degree in <a href="/wiki/Physical_education" title="Physical education">physical education</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-true_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-true-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Decathlon_career">Decathlon career</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">All mentioned Olympic events were men's events which took place prior to Jenner's gender transition.</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_career">Early career</span></h3>
<p>At the <a href="/wiki/1972_United_States_Olympic_Trials_(track_and_field)" title="1972 United States Olympic Trials (track and field)">1972 U.S. Olympic trials</a> in <a href="/wiki/Eugene,_Oregon" title="Eugene, Oregon">Eugene, Oregon</a>, Jenner was in fifth place in the men's decathlon, behind Steve Gough and Andrew Pettes, with only the last event remaining. Needing to make up a 19-second gap on Gough in the men's <a href="/wiki/1500_metres" title="1500 metres">1500 metres</a>, Jenner qualified for the Olympic team by running a fast final lap, finishing 22 seconds ahead of the other runners. This prompted the <i><a href="/wiki/Eugene_Register-Guard" class="mw-redirect" title="Eugene Register-Guard">Eugene Register-Guard</a></i> to ask: "Who's Jenner?"<sup id="cite_ref-zarnowski_1992_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zarnowski_1992-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-usot_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usot-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Following the Olympic Trials, Jenner finished in tenth place in the <a href="/wiki/Athletics_at_the_1972_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_decathlon" title="Athletics at the 1972 Summer Olympics – Men&#39;s decathlon">decathlon</a> at the <a href="/wiki/1972_Summer_Olympics" title="1972 Summer Olympics">1972 Summer Olympics</a> in <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-munchen_summer_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-munchen_summer-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> By watching Soviet <a href="/wiki/Mykola_Avilov" title="Mykola Avilov">Mykola Avilov</a> win the event, Jenner was inspired to start an intense training regimen. "For the first time, I knew what I wanted out of life and that was it, and this guy has it. I literally started training that night at midnight, running through the streets of Munich, Germany, training for the Games. I trained that day on through the 1976 Games, 6–8 hours a day, every day, 365 days a year."<sup id="cite_ref-espnoly_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-espnoly-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After graduating from Graceland, Jenner married girlfriend Chrystie Crownover and moved to <a href="/wiki/San_Jose,_California" title="San Jose, California">San Jose, California</a>. Crownover provided most of the family income by working as a flight attendant for <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Airlines</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-forgotten_history_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forgotten_history-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Jenner trained during the day and sold insurance at night, earning <span style="white-space: nowrap"><a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>9,000</span> a year.<sup id="cite_ref-OK!_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OK!-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ABC42415_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC42415-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> In the era before <a href="/wiki/Amateur_sports#Olympics" title="Amateur sports">professional American athletes</a> were allowed to compete in Olympic sports, this kind of training was unheard of. On the other hand, Soviet athletes were state-sponsored, which gave them a certain advantage over amateur American athletes.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> During this period, Jenner trained at the <a href="/wiki/San_Jose_City_College" title="San Jose City College">San Jose City College</a> (SJCC) and <a href="/wiki/San_Jose_State_University" title="San Jose State University">San Jose State University</a> (SJSU) tracks.<sup id="cite_ref-speed_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-speed-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-decathlon_hopeful_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-decathlon_hopeful-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> San Jose athletics centered on SJCC coach <a href="/wiki/Bert_Bonanno" title="Bert Bonanno">Bert Bonanno</a>; at that time, the city was a hotbed for training and was called the "Track Capital of the World".<sup id="cite_ref-ABC42415_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC42415-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Many other aspiring Olympic athletes also trained at San Jose; the list included <a href="/wiki/Millard_Hampton" title="Millard Hampton">Millard Hampton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andre_Phillips" title="Andre Phillips">Andre Phillips</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Powell_(athlete)" title="John Powell (athlete)">John Powell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mac_Wilkins" title="Mac Wilkins">Mac Wilkins</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Al_Feuerbach" title="Al Feuerbach">Al Feuerbach</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-speed_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-speed-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bj_wins_decathlon_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bj_wins_decathlon-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Jenner's most successful events were the skill events of the second day: hurdles, discus, pole vault, javelin and 1500 meters.<sup id="cite_ref-dmr_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dmr-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Sports_Book_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Sports_Book-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Olympic_success">Olympic success</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bruce_Jenner_discus_PanAm_1975.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Bruce_Jenner_discus_PanAm_1975.jpg/220px-Bruce_Jenner_discus_PanAm_1975.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Bruce_Jenner_discus_PanAm_1975.jpg/330px-Bruce_Jenner_discus_PanAm_1975.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Bruce_Jenner_discus_PanAm_1975.jpg/440px-Bruce_Jenner_discus_PanAm_1975.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1599" data-file-height="1269" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bruce_Jenner_discus_PanAm_1975.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Jenner at the 1975 Pan American Games</div></div></div>
<p>Jenner was the American champion in the men's decathlon event in 1974, and was featured on the cover of <i><a href="/wiki/Track_%26_Field_News" title="Track &amp; Field News">Track &amp; Field News</a></i> magazine's August 1974 issue.<sup id="cite_ref-1974_covers_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1974_covers-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-USA_TF_HOF_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USA_TF_HOF-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> While on tour in 1975, Jenner won the French national championship,<sup id="cite_ref-french_championships_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-french_championships-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> and a gold medal at the <a href="/wiki/1975_Pan_American_Games" title="1975 Pan American Games">1975 Pan American Games</a>, earning the tournament record with 8,045 points.<sup id="cite_ref-true_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-true-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> This was followed by <a href="/wiki/Decathlon_world_record_progression" title="Decathlon world record progression">new world records</a> of 8,524 points at the U.S.A./U.S.S.R./Poland triangular meet in Eugene, Oregon on August 9–10, 1975, breaking Avilov's record,<sup id="cite_ref-ghrecd_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ghrecd-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> and 8,538 points at the <a href="/wiki/1976_United_States_Olympic_Trials_(track_and_field)" title="1976 United States Olympic Trials (track and field)">1976 Olympic trials</a>, also in Eugene.<sup id="cite_ref-usot_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usot-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bohaend_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bohaend-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> The record in Eugene was a hybrid score because a <a href="/wiki/Fully_automatic_timing" class="mw-redirect" title="Fully automatic timing">timing system</a> failure and <a href="/wiki/Wind_assistance" title="Wind assistance">wind aided</a> marks. Still, Jenner was proud of "A nice little workout, huh?"
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886047036">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>"We got what we wanted. We scared the hell out of everybody in the world only a month away from the Games."<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<p>Of the 13 decathlons Jenner competed in between 1973 and 1976, the only loss was at the 1975 <a href="/wiki/Amateur_Athletic_Union" title="Amateur Athletic Union">AAU</a> National Championships, when a <a href="/wiki/Pole_vault#Modern_vaulting" title="Pole vault">"no height"</a> in the pole vault marred the score.<sup id="cite_ref-true_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-true-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the <a href="/wiki/Athletics_at_the_1976_Summer_Olympics" title="Athletics at the 1976 Summer Olympics">1976 Olympic Games</a> in <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a>, Jenner achieved five personal bests on the first day of the men's <a href="/wiki/Athletics_at_the_1976_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_decathlon" title="Athletics at the 1976 Summer Olympics – Men&#39;s decathlon">decathlon</a>&#160;&#8211;&#160;a "home run"&#160;&#8211;&#160;despite being in second place behind <a href="/wiki/Guido_Kratschmer" title="Guido Kratschmer">Guido Kratschmer</a> of <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West Germany</a>. Jenner was confident: "The second day has all my good events. If everything works out all right, we should be ahead after it's all over." Following a rainstorm on the second day, Jenner watched teammate <a href="/wiki/Fred_Dixon_(athlete)" title="Fred Dixon (athlete)">Fred Dixon</a> get injured in the <a href="/wiki/110_meter_hurdles" class="mw-redirect" title="110 meter hurdles">110 meter hurdles</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> so took a cautious approach to the hurdles and discus, then had personal bests in the pole vault, when Jenner took the lead, and javelin.<sup id="cite_ref-javelin_record_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-javelin_record-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> By that point, victory was virtually assured, but it remained to be seen by how much Jenner would improve the record. In the final event—the 1500 meters, which was seen live on national television—Jenner looked content to finish the long competition. Jenner sprinted the last lap, making up a 50-meter deficit and nearly catching the event favorite, Soviet <a href="/wiki/Leonid_Litvinenko" class="mw-redirect" title="Leonid Litvinenko">Leonid Litvinenko</a>, who was already well out of contention for the gold medal, but whose personal best had been eight seconds better than Jenner's personal best before the race. Jenner set a new personal best time and won the gold medal with a world-record score of 8,618 points.<sup id="cite_ref-dmr_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dmr-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-usot_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usot-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-espnoly_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-espnoly-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-athletics_at_the_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-athletics_at_the-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lhpowgwm_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lhpowgwm-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>Olympic world record performance</b>:<sup id="cite_ref-her_achievements_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-her_achievements-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><br />
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Impact">Impact</span></h3>
<p>After the event, Jenner took an American flag from a spectator and carried it during the victory lap, starting a tradition that is now common among winning athletes.<sup id="cite_ref-revisiting_bruce_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-revisiting_bruce-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-american_sports_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-american_sports-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Abandoning vaulting poles in the stadium, with no intention of ever competing again, Jenner stated that: "In 1972, I made the decision that I would go four years and totally dedicate myself to what I was doing, and then I would move on after it was over with. I went into that competition knowing that would be the last time I would ever do this."<sup id="cite_ref-espnoly_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-espnoly-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Jenner explained, "It hurts every day when you practice hard. Plus, when this decathlon is over, I got the rest of my life to recuperate. Who cares how bad it hurts?"<sup id="cite_ref-dmr_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dmr-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As a result of winning the Olympic decathlon, Jenner became a national hero and received the <a href="/wiki/James_E._Sullivan_Award" title="James E. Sullivan Award">James E. Sullivan Award</a> as the top amateur athlete in the United States and was also named the <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">Associated Press</a> Male Athlete of the Year in 1976.<sup id="cite_ref-giardina_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-giardina-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HolstPopp2004_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HolstPopp2004-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Jenner's 1976 world and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Olympic_records_in_athletics" title="List of Olympic records in athletics">Olympic record</a> was broken by four points by <a href="/wiki/Daley_Thompson" title="Daley Thompson">Daley Thompson</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Athletics_at_the_1980_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_decathlon" title="Athletics at the 1980 Summer Olympics – Men&#39;s decathlon">1980 Olympics</a> in <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a>; Thompson's victory was perhaps tainted by the U.S.-led boycott of the Moscow Olympics in protest of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_invasion_of_Afghanistan" class="mw-redirect" title="Soviet invasion of Afghanistan">Soviet invasion of Afghanistan</a>, though the top American at the time, <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Coffman" title="Bobby Coffman">Bobby Coffman</a>, was not expected to push Thompson or challenge Jenner's record. In 1985, Jenner's Olympic decathlon score was reevaluated against the <a href="/wiki/IAAF" class="mw-redirect" title="IAAF">IAAF</a>'s updated decathlon scoring table and was reported as 8,634 for comparative purposes. This converted mark stood as the American record until 1991, when it was surpassed by eventual gold medalist, and world record holder, <a href="/wiki/Dan_O%27Brien" title="Dan O&#39;Brien">Dan O'Brien</a> of <a href="/wiki/Dan_%26_Dave" title="Dan &amp; Dave">Dan &amp; Dave</a> fame.<sup id="cite_ref-dan_o_brien_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dan_o_brien-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> As of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Caitlyn_Jenner&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Jenner was ranked twenty-sixth on the world all-time list and ninth on the American all-time list.<sup id="cite_ref-all_time_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-all_time-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Jenner was inducted into the United States <a href="/wiki/National_Track_and_Field_Hall_of_Fame" title="National Track and Field Hall of Fame">National Track and Field Hall of Fame</a> in 1980, the Olympic Hall of Fame in 1986, the <a href="/wiki/Bay_Area_Sports_Hall_of_Fame" title="Bay Area Sports Hall of Fame">Bay Area Sports Hall of Fame</a> and the Connecticut Sports Hall of Fame in 1994, and the San Jose Sports Hall of Fame in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-arturs_irbe_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arturs_irbe-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> For almost 20 years, San Jose City College hosted an annual Bruce Jenner Invitational competition.<sup id="cite_ref-jenner_invitational_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jenner_invitational-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-my_connection_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-my_connection-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bud_winter_bio_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bud_winter_bio-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
