<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-Olympic_career">Post-Olympic career</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Capitalizing_on_Olympic_fame">Capitalizing on Olympic fame</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bruce_Jenner_greets_Gerald_Ford_and_William_Tolbert_in_1976_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Bruce_Jenner_greets_Gerald_Ford_and_William_Tolbert_in_1976_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Bruce_Jenner_greets_Gerald_Ford_and_William_Tolbert_in_1976_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Bruce_Jenner_greets_Gerald_Ford_and_William_Tolbert_in_1976_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Bruce_Jenner_greets_Gerald_Ford_and_William_Tolbert_in_1976_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Bruce_Jenner_greets_Gerald_Ford_and_William_Tolbert_in_1976_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Bruce_Jenner_greets_Gerald_Ford_and_William_Tolbert_in_1976_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="750" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bruce_Jenner_greets_Gerald_Ford_and_William_Tolbert_in_1976_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Jenner <i>(right)</i> greets Liberian president <a href="/wiki/William_Tolbert" title="William Tolbert">William Tolbert</a> <i>(left)</i> at the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a> on September 21, 1976, as United States President <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Ford" title="Gerald Ford">Gerald Ford</a> looks on</div></div></div>
<p>In the 1970s, Olympic athletes were considered to be amateurs and were not allowed to seek or accept payment for their positions as sports celebrities. During the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> in 1972, three major Olympic titles that had a long history of American success&#160;&#8211;&#160;<a href="/wiki/Basketball_at_the_1972_Summer_Olympics" title="Basketball at the 1972 Summer Olympics">basketball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Athletics_at_the_1972_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_100_metres" title="Athletics at the 1972 Summer Olympics – Men&#39;s 100 metres">the 100 meter dash</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Athletics_at_the_1972_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_decathlon" title="Athletics at the 1972 Summer Olympics – Men&#39;s decathlon">decathlon</a>&#160;&#8211;&#160;were won by <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> athletes. All Soviet athletes were professionals, while the United States was limited to amateurs.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_34-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_34-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Jenner became an American hero by returning the decathlon title to the United States. "After the Games were over," Jenner said, "I happened to be the right guy, at that right place, at that right time."<sup id="cite_ref-espnoly_29-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-espnoly-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tony_Kornheiser" title="Tony Kornheiser">Tony Kornheiser</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> wrote: "Jenner is twirling the nation like a baton. He and wife, Chrystie, are so high up on the pedestal of American heroism, it would take a crane to get them down."<sup id="cite_ref-dmr_5-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dmr-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-forgotten_history_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forgotten_history-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-spotlight_shifts_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spotlight_shifts-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After the expected Olympic success, Jenner planned to cash in on whatever celebrity status could follow a gold medal in the same mold as <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Weissmuller" title="Johnny Weissmuller">Johnny Weissmuller</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sonja_Henie" title="Sonja Henie">Sonja Henie</a>, who had become major movie stars following their gold medals. This would require forgoing any future Olympic competition. At the time, Jenner's agent George Wallach felt there was a four-year window&#160;&#8211;&#160;until the next Olympics&#160;&#8211;&#160;upon which to capitalize. Wallach reported that Jenner was being considered for the role of <i><a href="/wiki/Superman_(1978_film)" title="Superman (1978 film)">Superman</a></i>, which ultimately went to <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Reeve" title="Christopher Reeve">Christopher Reeve</a>. "I really don't know how many offers we have," Wallach claimed. "There are still unopened telegrams back at the hotel and you just can't believe the offers that poured in during the first two days."<sup id="cite_ref-nydn_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nydn-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Jenner appeared on the cover of the August 9, 1976, issue of <i><a href="/wiki/Sports_Illustrated" title="Sports Illustrated">Sports Illustrated</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-August_9,_1976_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-August_9,_1976-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> the February 1979 issue of <i><a href="/wiki/Gentleman%27s_Quarterly" class="mw-redirect" title="Gentleman&#39;s Quarterly">Gentleman's Quarterly</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-sexy_1979_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sexy_1979-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> and on the cover of <i>Playgirl</i> magazine.<sup id="cite_ref-formerly_bruce_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-formerly_bruce-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Jenner became a spokesperson for <a href="/wiki/Tropicana_Products" title="Tropicana Products">Tropicana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minolta" title="Minolta">Minolta</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Caleres" title="Caleres">Buster Brown shoes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-espnoly_29-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-espnoly-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Jenner was also selected by the <a href="/wiki/Sacramento_Kings" title="Sacramento Kings">Kansas City Kings</a> with the 139th overall pick in the seventh round of the <a href="/wiki/1977_NBA_draft" title="1977 NBA draft">1977 NBA draft</a> despite not having played basketball since high school.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Publicity_stunt" title="Publicity stunt">publicity stunt</a> was executed by team president/general manager <a href="/wiki/Joe_Axelson" title="Joe Axelson">Joe Axelson</a> to mock the <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City_Chiefs" title="Kansas City Chiefs">Kansas City Chiefs</a>' yearly claims that they planned on selecting "the best athlete available" in the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League_Draft" title="National Football League Draft">National Football League Draft</a>. Jenner was presented with a jersey customized with the number 8618, the Olympic-gold-medal-winning score, but would never appear as an active player with the Kings.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Wheaties_spokesperson">Wheaties spokesperson</span></h4>
<p><span id="Wheaties"></span>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jenner_on_Wheaties_cereal_box.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/5c/Jenner_on_Wheaties_cereal_box.jpg/170px-Jenner_on_Wheaties_cereal_box.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="262" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/5/5c/Jenner_on_Wheaties_cereal_box.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="254" data-file-height="392" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jenner_on_Wheaties_cereal_box.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Wheaties" title="Wheaties">Wheaties</a> boxes featuring Jenner came out around the same time the athlete became a spokesperson for the breakfast cereal. A box would later sell on eBay for <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$400</span> after she announced her transition in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-wheaties_for_hundreds_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wheaties_for_hundreds-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-unopened_box_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unopened_box-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>In 1977, Jenner became a spokesperson for <a href="/wiki/Wheaties" title="Wheaties">Wheaties</a> brand breakfast cereal and appeared in a photograph on the cover of the cereal box. After taking over from Olympic champion <a href="/wiki/Bob_Richards" title="Bob Richards">Bob Richards</a>, Jenner was second in a succession of athletes featured as spokespersons for the brand. <a href="/wiki/Mary_Lou_Retton" title="Mary Lou Retton">Mary Lou Retton</a> succeeded Jenner in 1984.<sup id="cite_ref-the_box_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-the_box-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On November 22, 1977, Jenner went to San Francisco to refute charges filed by <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_District_Attorney%27s_Office" title="San Francisco District Attorney&#39;s Office">San Francisco district attorney</a> Joseph Freitas that <a href="/wiki/General_Mills" title="General Mills">General Mills</a>—the maker of Wheaties—had engaged in deceptive advertising in its campaign that featured Jenner. Jenner liked Wheaties and ate the breakfast cereal two or three times a week, which supported the advertising campaign's claims. Two days later, Freitas withdrew the suit, saying that it was "a case of overzealousness" on the part of his staff.<sup id="cite_ref-defend_boc_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-defend_boc-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>When Jenner came out as a trans woman in 2015, General Mills stated that: "Bruce Jenner continues to be a respected member of Team Wheaties." After a negative response to this initial statement, Mike Siemienas, General Mills's brand media relations manager, clarified it by saying: "Bruce Jenner has been a respected member of Team Wheaties, and Caitlyn Jenner will continue to be."<sup id="cite_ref-strange_response_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-strange_response-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Television_and_film_career">Television and film career</span></h3>
<p>The comedy <i><a href="/wiki/Can%27t_Stop_the_Music" title="Can&#39;t Stop the Music">Can't Stop the Music</a></i> (1980) was Jenner's only theatrical release until 2011. Jenner had some success with a television career, starring in the made-for-TV movies <i>The Golden Moment: An Olympic Love Story</i><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> (1980) and <i><a href="/wiki/Grambling%27s_White_Tiger" title="Grambling&#39;s White Tiger">Grambling's White Tiger</a></i> (1981).<sup id="cite_ref-white_tiger_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-white_tiger-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> During the 1981–1982 season, Jenner became a semi-regular cast member in the police series <i><a href="/wiki/CHiPs" title="CHiPs">CHiPs</a></i>, guest-starring as Officer Steve McLeish for six episodes, substituting for star <a href="/wiki/Erik_Estrada" title="Erik Estrada">Erik Estrada</a>, who was locked in a contract dispute with <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a> and <a href="/wiki/MGM" class="mw-redirect" title="MGM">MGM</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-KindelanEffron_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KindelanEffron-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Jenner also appeared in an episode of the sitcom <i><a href="/wiki/Silver_Spoons" title="Silver Spoons">Silver Spoons</a></i> called "Trouble with Words", wherein her personal issues with dyslexia were revealed in a storyline about a recurring teenage character with the same problem.
</p><p>Jenner appeared in the series <i><a href="/wiki/Learn_to_Read" title="Learn to Read">Learn to Read</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> and in the video games <i><a href="/wiki/Olympic_Decathlon" title="Olympic Decathlon">Olympic Decathlon</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-gamefaqs_1996_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gamefaqs_1996-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> (1981) and <i><a href="/wiki/Bruce_Jenner%27s_World_Class_Decathlon" title="Bruce Jenner&#39;s World Class Decathlon">Bruce Jenner's World Class Decathlon</a></i> (1996).<sup id="cite_ref-gamefaqs_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gamefaqs-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> The "hero shot", the finish of the final event of the 1976 Olympic decathlon, and the Wheaties cover, were parodied by <a href="/wiki/John_Belushi" title="John Belushi">John Belushi</a> on <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live" title="Saturday Night Live">Saturday Night Live</a></i>, endorsing "Little Chocolate Donuts".<sup id="cite_ref-snl_season_3_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-snl_season_3-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> In 1989, Jenner played herself in the comedy short <i><a href="/wiki/Dirty_Tennis" title="Dirty Tennis">Dirty Tennis</a></i> written by <a href="/wiki/James_Van_Patten" class="mw-redirect" title="James Van Patten">James Van Patten</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-dirty_tennis_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dirty_tennis-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bruce_Jenner_1996.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Bruce_Jenner_1996.jpg/170px-Bruce_Jenner_1996.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="224" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Bruce_Jenner_1996.jpg/255px-Bruce_Jenner_1996.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Bruce_Jenner_1996.jpg/340px-Bruce_Jenner_1996.jpg 2x" data-file-width="805" data-file-height="1059" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bruce_Jenner_1996.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Jenner in 1996</div></div></div>
<p>Jenner has appeared in a variety of <a href="/wiki/Game_show" title="Game show">game shows</a> and <a href="/wiki/Reality_television" title="Reality television">reality television</a> programs, including starring with <a href="/wiki/Grits_Gresham" title="Grits Gresham">Grits Gresham</a> in an episode of <i><a href="/wiki/The_American_Sportsman" title="The American Sportsman">The American Sportsman</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-cj_bio_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cj_bio-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> In the early 1990s, Jenner was the host of an <a href="/wiki/Infomercial" title="Infomercial">infomercial</a> for a stair-climbing exercise machine called the Stair Climber Plus.<sup id="cite_ref-super_step_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-super_step-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2002, Jenner participated in an episode of the American series <i><a href="/wiki/Weakest_Link_(U.S._game_show)" class="mw-redirect" title="Weakest Link (U.S. game show)">The Weakest Link</a></i>, featuring Olympic athletes.<sup id="cite_ref-weakest_link_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-weakest_link-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> In February and March 2003, Jenner was part of the cast of the American series <i><a href="/wiki/I%27m_a_Celebrity...Get_Me_Out_of_Here!" title="I&#39;m a Celebrity...Get Me Out of Here!">I'm a Celebrity...Get Me Out of Here!</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-get_me_out_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-get_me_out-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> She made a cameo appearance in a season-three episode of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Apprentice_(U.S._season_3)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Apprentice (U.S. season 3)">The Apprentice</a></i>, which aired in May 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-the_apprentice_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-the_apprentice-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> She also partnered with <a href="/wiki/Tai_Babilonia" title="Tai Babilonia">Tai Babilonia</a> for <i><a href="/wiki/Skating_with_Celebrities" title="Skating with Celebrities">Skating with Celebrities</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-skating_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-skating-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> in a series that aired January&#160;&#8211;&#160;March 2006 (they were eliminated during the fifth of seven episodes), served as a guest judge on <i><a href="/wiki/Pet_Star" title="Pet Star">Pet Star</a></i> on <a href="/wiki/Animal_Planet" title="Animal Planet">Animal Planet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pet_star_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pet_star-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> In November 2010, a photograph of Jenner was shown in a janitor's resume in an episode of <i><a href="/wiki/It%27s_Always_Sunny_in_Philadelphia" title="It&#39;s Always Sunny in Philadelphia">It's Always Sunny in Philadelphia</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-always_sunny_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-always_sunny-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Additional television and talk show appearances by Jenner include: <a href="/wiki/Nickelodeon" title="Nickelodeon">Nickelodeon</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Made-for-TV" class="mw-redirect" title="Made-for-TV">made-for-TV</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/Gym_Teacher:_The_Movie" title="Gym Teacher: The Movie">Gym Teacher: The Movie</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-gym_teacher_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gym_teacher-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> as well as episodes of <i><a href="/wiki/Murder,_She_Wrote" title="Murder, She Wrote">Murder, She Wrote</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-awesome_timing_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-awesome_timing-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> the <i><a href="/wiki/Lingo_(U.S._game_show)" class="mw-redirect" title="Lingo (U.S. game show)">Lingo</a></i> Olympic Winners episode,<sup id="cite_ref-dyslexic_olympian_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dyslexic_olympian-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> and talk shows such as <i><a href="/wiki/Hannity" title="Hannity">Hannity</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-tinseltown_conservatives_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tinseltown_conservatives-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> and season<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>1, episode<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>21 of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Bonnie_Hunt_Show" title="The Bonnie Hunt Show">The Bonnie Hunt Show</a></i> in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-bhs_season_1_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bhs_season_1-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since late 2007, Jenner has starred in the <a href="/wiki/E!" title="E!">E!</a> reality series <i><a href="/wiki/Keeping_Up_with_the_Kardashians" title="Keeping Up with the Kardashians">Keeping Up with the Kardashians</a></i> along with wife <a href="/wiki/Kris_Jenner" title="Kris Jenner">Kris Jenner</a>, stepchildren Kourtney, Kimberley, Khloé, and Rob Kardashian (from Kris's marriage to attorney <a href="/wiki/Robert_Kardashian" title="Robert Kardashian">Robert Kardashian</a>), and daughters Kylie and Kendall.<sup id="cite_ref-jenner_split_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jenner_split-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2011, Jenner appeared in the <a href="/wiki/Adam_Sandler" title="Adam Sandler">Adam Sandler</a> comedy <i><a href="/wiki/Jack_and_Jill_(2011_film)" title="Jack and Jill (2011 film)">Jack and Jill</a></i> in a scene with <a href="/wiki/Al_Pacino" title="Al Pacino">Al Pacino</a> as an actor in a play.<sup id="cite_ref-jack_and_jill_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jack_and_jill-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> Like <i>Can't Stop the Music</i>, the film won the Golden Raspberry Award for Worst Picture and swept every Razzie category.<sup id="cite_ref-new_razzie_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-new_razzie-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2016, Jenner appeared as herself on the Amazon Prime TV series <i><a href="/wiki/Transparent_(TV_series)" title="Transparent (TV series)">Transparent</a></i> in a dream sequence during the season three episode "To Sardines and Back".<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Motorsports_career">Motorsports career</span></h3>
<p>Jenner had a short career as a race car driver in the <a href="/wiki/IMSA_GT_Championship" title="IMSA GT Championship">IMSA Camel GT series</a> (<a href="/wiki/International_Motor_Sports_Association" title="International Motor Sports Association">International Motor Sports Association</a>) in the 1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-Nelson_p612_2013_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nelson_p612_2013-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> Jenner's first victory came in the <a href="/wiki/1986_IMSA_GT_Championship_season" class="mw-redirect" title="1986 IMSA GT Championship season">1986</a> <a href="/wiki/12_hours_of_Sebring" class="mw-redirect" title="12 hours of Sebring">12 hours of Sebring</a> in the IMSA GTO class driving the <a href="/wiki/7-Eleven" title="7-Eleven">7-Eleven</a> <a href="/wiki/Roush_Racing" class="mw-redirect" title="Roush Racing">Roush Racing</a> <a href="/wiki/Ford_Mustang" title="Ford Mustang">Ford Mustang</a> with co-driver <a href="/wiki/Scott_Pruett" title="Scott Pruett">Scott Pruett</a>. The pair won their class and finished 4th overall in the 12-hour endurance race. 1986 was also the most successful year of Jenner's career, finishing second in the championship to Pruett.<sup id="cite_ref-scott_pruett_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scott_pruett-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-imsa_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imsa-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Jenner commented, "I was a lot more badass runner than I was a driver."<sup id="cite_ref-yahoo_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yahoo-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Business">Business</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Web_Summit_2017_-_Centre_Stage_Day_3_DF2_7286_(38286777521).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Web_Summit_2017_-_Centre_Stage_Day_3_DF2_7286_%2838286777521%29.jpg/220px-Web_Summit_2017_-_Centre_Stage_Day_3_DF2_7286_%2838286777521%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Web_Summit_2017_-_Centre_Stage_Day_3_DF2_7286_%2838286777521%29.jpg/330px-Web_Summit_2017_-_Centre_Stage_Day_3_DF2_7286_%2838286777521%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Web_Summit_2017_-_Centre_Stage_Day_3_DF2_7286_%2838286777521%29.jpg/440px-Web_Summit_2017_-_Centre_Stage_Day_3_DF2_7286_%2838286777521%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4013" data-file-height="2715" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Web_Summit_2017_-_Centre_Stage_Day_3_DF2_7286_(38286777521).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Jenner at the <a href="/wiki/Web_Summit" title="Web Summit">Web Summit</a> 2017, in <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a></div></div></div>
<p>Jenner had licensed her previous name for <i>Bruce Jenner's Westwood Centers for Nautilus &amp; Aerobics</i> in the early 1980s to David A. Cirotto, president of other local Nautilus &amp; Aerobics Centers. She had no ownership in the licensed name centers,<sup id="cite_ref-OK!_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OK!-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> which were solely owned by Cirotto.<sup id="cite_ref-health_club_suit_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-health_club_suit-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> Jenner's company, Bruce Jenner Aviation, sells aircraft supplies to executives and corporations.<sup id="cite_ref-OK!_31-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OK!-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Jenner was the business development vice president for a staffing industry software application known as JennerNet, which was based on Lotus Domino technology.<sup id="cite_ref-san_rafael_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-san_rafael-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2016, Jenner announced that she had been chosen as the face of <a href="/wiki/H%26M" title="H&amp;M">H&amp;M</a> Sport.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Later that year, H&amp;M created a six-minute film featuring Jenner, called <i>Caitlyn Jenner's Greatest Victories: A Timeline</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Gender_transition">Gender transition</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Coming_out_as_a_transgender_woman">Coming out as a transgender woman</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:VanityFairJuly2015.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1d/VanityFairJuly2015.jpg/170px-VanityFairJuly2015.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="238" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/1/1d/VanityFairJuly2015.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="214" data-file-height="300" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:VanityFairJuly2015.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>The Washington Post</i> commented that Jenner's debut <i><a href="/wiki/Vanity_Fair_(magazine)" title="Vanity Fair (magazine)">Vanity Fair</a></i> cover, shot by <a href="/wiki/Annie_Leibovitz" title="Annie Leibovitz">Annie Leibovitz</a>, had special significance for its subject: "After all the magazine covers that featured the former athlete, once lauded as the 'world's greatest athlete,' the Leibovitz photograph will be the most meaningful. Looking directly at the camera, Jenner is finally herself for the first time publicly."<sup id="cite_ref-world&#39;s_greatest_athlete_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-world&#39;s_greatest_athlete-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-capehart_2015_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-capehart_2015-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>In a <i><a href="/wiki/20/20_(U.S._TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="20/20 (U.S. TV series)">20/20</a></i> interview with <a href="/wiki/Diane_Sawyer" title="Diane Sawyer">Diane Sawyer</a> in April 2015, Jenner <a href="/wiki/Came_out" class="mw-redirect" title="Came out">came out</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Trans_woman" title="Trans woman">trans woman</a>, saying that she had dealt with <a href="/wiki/Gender_dysphoria" title="Gender dysphoria">gender dysphoria</a> since her youth and that, "for all intents and purposes, I'm a woman." Jenner <a href="/wiki/Cross-dressing" title="Cross-dressing">cross-dressed</a> for many years and took <a href="/wiki/Hormone_replacement_therapy_(male-to-female)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hormone replacement therapy (male-to-female)">hormone replacement therapy</a> but stopped after her romance with <a href="/wiki/Kris_Jenner" title="Kris Jenner">Kris Kardashian</a> became more serious, leading to marriage in 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-DooleyDawson_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DooleyDawson-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-trans2_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trans2-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EstherLee_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EstherLee-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> Jenner recounts having permission to explore her gender identity on her own travels but not when they were coupled, and that not knowing the best way to talk about the many issues contributed to the deterioration of the 23-year-long marriage, which ended formally in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-EstherLee_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EstherLee-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Jenner has undergone cosmetic surgery, and completed <a href="/wiki/Sex_reassignment_surgery_(male-to-female)" title="Sex reassignment surgery (male-to-female)">sex reassignment surgery</a> in January 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> She said she has never been sexually attracted to men, but always to women, and that, keeping in mind the difficulty people have understanding the difference between <a href="/wiki/Sexual_orientation" title="Sexual orientation">sexual orientation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gender_identity" title="Gender identity">gender identity</a>, she will identify as <a href="/wiki/Asexuality" title="Asexuality">asexual</a> for now.<sup id="cite_ref-Yahr_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahr-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-celebrities_reacted_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-celebrities_reacted-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_attention">Media attention</span></h3>
<p>In June 2015, Jenner debuted her new name and image, and began publicly using feminine pronoun self-descriptors.<sup id="cite_ref-introducing_caitlyn_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-introducing_caitlyn-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> Jenner held a renaming ceremony in July 2015, adopting the name Caitlyn Marie Jenner.<sup id="cite_ref-i_am_cait_2015_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-i_am_cait_2015-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-renaming_ceremony_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-renaming_ceremony-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> Prior to her <i>20/20</i> interview, a two-part special titled <i>Keeping Up with the Kardashians: About Bruce</i> was filmed with the family in which she answered questions, and prepared her children for the personal and public aspects of the transition. In the special, which aired in May 2015, the point was emphasized that there is no one right way to transition. Jenner made it a priority to ensure that all her children were independent first before focusing on her transition.<sup id="cite_ref-MarcusStephanie_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MarcusStephanie-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> In September 2015, her name was legally changed to Caitlyn Marie Jenner and gender to female.<sup id="cite_ref-judge_grants_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-judge_grants-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Jenner's announcement that she is transgender came at an unprecedented time for trans visibility, including <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_the_United_States" title="LGBT rights in the United States">legislative initiatives</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Griggs_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Griggs-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Helmore_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Helmore-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> The <i>20/20</i> interview had 20.7 million viewers, making it television's "highest-ever rated newsmagazine telecast among adults 18–49 and adults 25–54".<sup id="cite_ref-marc_berman_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marc_berman-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Beast" title="The Daily Beast">The Daily Beast</a></i> wrote that Jenner's honesty, vulnerability, and fame may have caused "cheap jokes" about trans people to "seem mean to a mainstream audience on an unprecedented scale".<sup id="cite_ref-Allen_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Allen-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> Noting the shift in how comedians treated Jenner's transition, <i>The Daily Beast</i> saw the change as the same evolution that took place in acceptance of <a href="/wiki/LGBT" title="LGBT">LGBT</a> people as a whole when "comedians finally cross the critical threshold from mockery to creativity in their joke-telling".<sup id="cite_ref-Allen_120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Allen-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Jenner's emerging gender identity was revealed in a <i>Vanity Fair</i> interview written by <a href="/wiki/Buzz_Bissinger" title="Buzz Bissinger">Buzz Bissinger</a>. <a href="/wiki/Annie_Leibovitz" title="Annie Leibovitz">Annie Leibovitz</a> photographed the cover, the magazine's first to feature an openly transgender woman, which was captioned "Call me Caitlyn".<sup id="cite_ref-pose_for_cover_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pose_for_cover-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-women_of_color_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-women_of_color-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> Using her <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> handle, @Caitlyn_Jenner, she tweeted: "I'm so happy after such a long struggle to be living my true self. Welcome to the world Caitlyn. Can't wait for you to get to know her/me." <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> magazine declared this tweet the tenth most re-tweeted tweet of 2015, based on re-tweets of tweets by verified users from January 1 to November 10 of that year.<sup id="cite_ref-retweeted_tweets_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-retweeted_tweets-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> Jenner amassed over one million Twitter followers in four hours and three minutes, setting a new <a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Record" class="mw-redirect" title="Guinness World Record">Guinness World Record</a> and surpassing United States President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>, who, a month before, accomplished the same feat in four hours and fifty-two minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-by_the_numbers_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-by_the_numbers-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-world_record_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-world_record-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> Four days later Jenner was up to 2.37 million followers, with another 1.5 million followers on <a href="/wiki/Instagram" title="Instagram">Instagram</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-graydon_carter_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-graydon_carter-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Jenner was also mocked. Beginning in September 2015, she was depicted on the satirical American animated program <i>South Park</i>, which parodied her supporters' <a href="/wiki/Political_correctness" title="Political correctness">political correctness</a>, as well as her driving record. The Jenner-related episodes were "<a href="/wiki/Stunning_and_Brave" title="Stunning and Brave">Stunning and Brave</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Where_My_Country_Gone%3F" title="Where My Country Gone?">Where My Country Gone?</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Sponsored_Content_(South_Park)" title="Sponsored Content (South Park)">Sponsored Content</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Truth_and_Advertising" title="Truth and Advertising">Truth and Advertising</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/PC_Principal_Final_Justice" title="PC Principal Final Justice">PC Principal Final Justice</a>" from the show's <a href="/wiki/South_Park_(season_19)" title="South Park (season 19)">19th season</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-south_park_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-south_park-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-south_park_ad_block_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-south_park_ad_block-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2016 during the <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_presidential_primaries,_2016" class="mw-redirect" title="Republican Party presidential primaries, 2016">Republican presidential primaries</a>, Jenner became an <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/exemplar" class="extiw" title="wikt:exemplar">exemplar</a> for candidate <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a>'s opposition to North Carolina's <a href="/wiki/Public_Facilities_Privacy_%26_Security_Act" title="Public Facilities Privacy &amp; Security Act">Public Facilities Privacy &amp; Security Act</a>, with Trump saying that Jenner could use any restroom of her choosing at his <a href="/wiki/Trump_Tower" title="Trump Tower">Trump Tower</a> property. Jenner soon posted a video showing that she had taken Trump up on his offer. She thanked Trump and assured Trump's adversary <a href="/wiki/Ted_Cruz" title="Ted Cruz">Ted Cruz</a> that "nobody got molested".<sup id="cite_ref-cudgel_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cudgel-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-trump_tower_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trump_tower-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2016, Jenner was one of several celebrities depicted using synthetic nude "sleeping" bodies for the video of <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a>'s song "<a href="/wiki/Famous_(Kanye_West_song)" title="Famous (Kanye West song)">Famous</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> Later that month, an episode of <i><a href="/wiki/Epic_Rap_Battles_of_History" title="Epic Rap Battles of History">Epic Rap Battles of History</a></i> was released featuring Jenner, as Bruce (portrayed by <a href="/wiki/Peter_Shukoff" title="Peter Shukoff">Peter Shukoff</a>) and then Caitlyn (portrayed by transgender rapper Jolie "NoShame" Drake), rap battling against <a href="/wiki/Hulk" title="Hulk">The Hulk</a> (portrayed by <a href="/wiki/Lloyd_Ahlquist" title="Lloyd Ahlquist">Lloyd Ahlquist</a>).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="General">General</span></h4>
<p>In August 2015, Jenner won the Social Media Queen award at the <a href="/wiki/Teen_Choice_Awards" title="Teen Choice Awards">Teen Choice Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-teen_choice_2015_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-teen_choice_2015-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> In October 2015, <i><a href="/wiki/Glamour_(magazine)" title="Glamour (magazine)">Glamour</a></i> magazine named her one of its 25 Glamour Women of the Year, calling her a "Trans Champion."<sup id="cite_ref-trans_champion_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trans_champion-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> In November 2015, Jenner was listed as one of <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> 2015 Entertainers of the Year.<sup id="cite_ref-ew_2015_eoty_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ew_2015_eoty-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> In December 2015, she was named <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Walters" title="Barbara Walters">Barbara Walters</a>' <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Walters%27_10_Most_Fascinating_People" title="Barbara Walters&#39; 10 Most Fascinating People">Most Fascinating Person</a> of 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-most_fascinating_2015_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-most_fascinating_2015-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> Also in that month, she was listed on <i>Time</i> magazine's eight-person shortlist for the 2015 Person of the Year,<sup id="cite_ref-time_poty_2015_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-time_poty_2015-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Bing_(search_engine)" title="Bing (search engine)">Bing</a> released its list of the year's "Most Searched Celebrities", which Jenner was at the top of, and declared Jenner's <i>Vanity Fair</i> cover the second in a list of "top celeb moments of 2015."<sup id="cite_ref-bing_top_2015_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bing_top_2015-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bing_most_2015_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bing_most_2015-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> She was the second most searched for person on <a href="/wiki/Google_Search" title="Google Search">Google</a> in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-google_10_most_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-google_10_most-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> In April 2016, she was listed in the <a href="/wiki/Time_100" title="Time 100"><i>Time</i> 100</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-wayne_maines_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wayne_maines-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> In June 2016, Jenner became the first openly transgender person to be featured on the cover of <i><a href="/wiki/Sports_Illustrated" title="Sports Illustrated">Sports Illustrated</a>.</i> The cover and associated story marked the 40th anniversary of her winning the <a href="/wiki/1976_Summer_Olympics" title="1976 Summer Olympics">1976 Summer Olympics</a> decathlon.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Feminist author <a href="/wiki/Germaine_Greer" title="Germaine Greer">Germaine Greer</a> called <i>Glamour</i> magazine's decision to award Jenner with a "Woman of the Year" award misogynistic, questioning whether a transgender woman could be better than "someone who is just born a woman."<sup id="cite_ref-wanted_limelight_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wanted_limelight-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> Jenner also received criticism from individuals such as actress <a href="/wiki/Rose_McGowan" title="Rose McGowan">Rose McGowan</a>, for stating&#160;&#8211;&#160;in a <a href="/wiki/BuzzFeed" title="BuzzFeed">BuzzFeed</a> interview<sup id="cite_ref-most_proud_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-most_proud-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>&#160;&#8211;&#160; that the hardest part about being a woman "is figuring out what to wear". McGowan argued: "We are more than deciding what to wear. We are more than the stereotypes foisted upon us by people like you. You're a woman now? Well fucking learn that we have had a VERY different experience than your life of male privilege." McGowan later stated that she was not transphobic, and added: "Disliking something a trans person has said is no different than disliking something a man has said or that a woman has said. Being trans doesn't make one immune from criticism."<sup id="cite_ref-Hetter_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hetter-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mcgowan-advocate_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mcgowan-advocate-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Chris Mandle of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">The Independent</a></i> stated: "Jenner has gone on to inspire countless men and women, but her comments, which were made after she was celebrated at <i>Glamour</i> magazine's Women Of The Year in New York were branded 'offensive and insulting'." He added: "People began tweeting the other, harder things women have to deal with, such as institutionalized oppression, abuse and sexual assault".<sup id="cite_ref-Mandle_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mandle-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> James Smith, husband of <a href="/wiki/Moira_Smith" class="mw-redirect" title="Moira Smith">Moira Smith</a>, the only female New York Police Department officer to die on September 11, 2001, returned Moira's "Woman of the Year" award, given posthumously. Referring to Jenner as a man, he stated that he found <i>Glamour</i> giving Jenner the same award insulting to Moira's memory, and referred to the matter as a publicity stunt.<sup id="cite_ref-heros_husband_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heros_husband-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-returns_award_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-returns_award-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> Smith later said that, having supported transgender youth and <i>Glamour</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> decision to honor transgender actress <a href="/wiki/Laverne_Cox" title="Laverne Cox">Laverne Cox</a> in 2014, he did not object because Jenner is transgender; he objected to Jenner's "hardest part about being a woman" commentary; this proved to him that Jenner "is not truly a woman. I believe this comment and others he has made trivializes the transgender experience as I have witnessed it."<sup id="cite_ref-Hetter_2_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hetter_2-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Conversely, Adrienne Tam of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a></i> argued that Jenner deserved the <i>Glamour</i> award, stating: "What McGowan failed to take into consideration was the jesting manner in which Jenner spoke." Tam said:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886047036"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>[Jenner] also immediately followed up her "what women wear" dilemma with: It's more than that. I'm kind of at this point in my life where I'm trying to figure this womanhood thing out. It is more than hair, makeup, clothes, all that kind of stuff. There's an element here that I'm still kind of searching for. And I think that'll take a while. Because I think as far as gender, we're all on a journey. We're all learning and growing about ourselves. And I feel the same way.
</p></blockquote>
<p>Tam considered McGowan's criticism to be over the top, and stated of James Smith's criticism, "The salient point here is one about courage. We easily recognise physical courage such as saving orphans from burning buildings, or ordinary people putting their lives in the line of fire. It is far harder to recognise mental courage." She added: "Without a doubt, the police officer who died in the September 11 attacks was courageous. But so is Jenner. It's a different kind of courage, but it is courage nonetheless."<sup id="cite_ref-Tam_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tam-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="LGBT_community">LGBT community</span></h4>
<p>Since coming out as a trans woman in 2015, Jenner has been called the most famous openly transgender woman in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-legal_name_change_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-legal_name_change-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Pilkington_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pilkington-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Transgender_reality_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Transgender_reality-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> She is also one of the most recognized LGBT people in the world and arguably the most famous <a href="/wiki/LGBT_Olympians" class="mw-redirect" title="LGBT Olympians">LGBT athlete</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-five_transgender_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-five_transgender-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> Jenner acknowledged in her <i>20/20</i> interview that part of her reason for being so visible was to bring attention to gender dysphoria, violence against trans women, and other <a href="/wiki/List_of_transgender-related_topics" title="List of transgender-related topics">transgender issues</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FordMatt_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FordMatt-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> She also sought to promote more informed discussion of LGBT issues at a time when the trans community has unprecedented visibility.<sup id="cite_ref-FordMatt_153-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FordMatt-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> She signed with <a href="/wiki/Creative_Artists_Agency" title="Creative Artists Agency">Creative Artists Agency</a>'s speakers department and will collaborate with the CAA Foundation on a philanthropic strategy focusing on LGBT issues.<sup id="cite_ref-caa_speakers_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-caa_speakers-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> She made a private appearance at the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_LGBT_Center" title="Los Angeles LGBT Center">Los Angeles LGBT Center</a> in June 2015, where she spoke with at-risk trans youth.<sup id="cite_ref-trans_youth_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trans_youth-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Jenner received the <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Ashe_Courage_Award" title="Arthur Ashe Courage Award">Arthur Ashe Courage Award</a> during the <a href="/wiki/2015_ESPY_Awards" title="2015 ESPY Awards">2015</a> <a href="/wiki/ESPY_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="ESPY Awards">ESPY Awards</a> in July 2015. ESPN executive producer Maura Mandt said Jenner was given the award because "she has shown the courage to embrace a truth that had been hidden for years, and to embark on a journey that may not only give comfort to those facing similar circumstances, but can also help to educate people on the challenges that the transgender community faces."<sup id="cite_ref-arthur_ashe_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arthur_ashe-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> She is the third consecutive openly LGBT person to receive the award following footballer <a href="/wiki/Michael_Sam" title="Michael Sam">Michael Sam</a> (2014) and anchorwoman <a href="/wiki/Robin_Roberts_(newscaster)" title="Robin Roberts (newscaster)">Robin Roberts</a> (2013).<sup id="cite_ref-watershed_moment_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-watershed_moment-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October, Jenner presented the <a href="/wiki/Point_Foundation_(LGBT)" title="Point Foundation (LGBT)">Point Foundation's</a> Horizon Award to television producers Rhys Ernst (of the show <i><a href="/wiki/Transparent_(TV_series)" title="Transparent (TV series)">Transparent</a></i>) and Zach Zyskowski (of the show <i><a href="/wiki/Becoming_Us" title="Becoming Us">Becoming Us</a></i>).<sup id="cite_ref-cleavage_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cleavage-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-suntimes1_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-suntimes1-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> This was her second public speaking engagement after her gender transition.<sup id="cite_ref-suntimes1_159-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-suntimes1-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November, Jenner was listed as one of the nine runners-up for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Advocate_(LGBT_magazine)" title="The Advocate (LGBT magazine)">The Advocate</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> Person of the Year.<sup id="cite_ref-the_finalists_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-the_finalists-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> That month she was also listed as one of the <i><a href="/wiki/Out_(magazine)" title="Out (magazine)">Out100</a></i> of 2015, with <i>Out</i> calling her the "Newsmaker of the Year."<sup id="cite_ref-out100_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-out100-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> On <a href="/wiki/International_Human_Rights_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="International Human Rights Day">International Human Rights Day</a>, Jenner discussed transgender rights with <a href="/wiki/Samantha_Power" title="Samantha Power">Samantha Power</a>, the U.S. Ambassador to the United Nations.<sup id="cite_ref-talks_transgender_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-talks_transgender-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> In 2016, Jenner was on the cover of <i>The Advocate</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> February/March issue.<sup id="cite_ref-education_of_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-education_of-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/MAC_Cosmetics" title="MAC Cosmetics">MAC Cosmetics</a> collaborated with Jenner on a lipstick, called Finally Free, which was made available for purchase April 8, 2016, with MAC stating, "100% of the selling price goes to the <a href="/wiki/MAC_AIDS_Fund" class="mw-redirect" title="MAC AIDS Fund">MAC AIDS Fund</a> Transgender Initiative, to further its work in support of transgender communities."<sup id="cite_ref-instagram_reveal_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-instagram_reveal-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mac_lipstick_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mac_lipstick-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> Also in April 2016, Jenner was listed as No.<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>8 on <i>Out</i> magazine's Power 50 list.<sup id="cite_ref-power_list_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-power_list-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-power_50_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-power_50-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> In May 2016, her interview with Diane Sawyer in 2015 won Outstanding TV Journalism&#160;&#8211;&#160;Newsmagazine at the <a href="/wiki/GLAAD_Media_Award" title="GLAAD Media Award">GLAAD Media Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-glaad_media_awards_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-glaad_media_awards-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2016, the <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Campaign" title="Human Rights Campaign">Human Rights Campaign</a> released a video in tribute to the victims of the <a href="/wiki/2016_Orlando_nightclub_shooting" class="mw-redirect" title="2016 Orlando nightclub shooting">2016 Orlando gay nightclub shooting</a>; in the video, Jenner and others told the stories of the people killed there.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2016, Jenner spoke about coming out as transgender and Republican at a <a href="/wiki/2016_Republican_National_Convention" title="2016 Republican National Convention">Republican National Convention</a> "Big Tent Brunch" for the conservative group American Unity Fund.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Show_and_memoir">Show and memoir</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/I_Am_Cait" title="I Am Cait">I Am Cait</a></div>
<p>Jenner's gender transition is the subject of <i>I Am Cait</i>, initially an eight-part TV documentary series, which premiered on E! in July 2015 to an audience of 2.7 million viewers.<sup id="cite_ref-docu-series_1st_promo_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-docu-series_1st_promo-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-docu-series_hits_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-docu-series_hits-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-heaps_of_praise_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heaps_of_praise-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> Jenner is an executive producer of the show.<sup id="cite_ref-joe_otterson_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-joe_otterson-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> The show focuses on Jenner's transition and how it affects her relationships with her family and friends. The show also explores how Jenner adjusts to what she sees as her job as a role model for the transgender community.<sup id="cite_ref-docu-series_promo_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-docu-series_promo-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-the_new_normal_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-the_new_normal-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> In October 2015, the show was renewed for a second season, which premiered on March 6, 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> The show tied for Outstanding Reality Program at the <a href="/wiki/GLAAD_Media_Award" title="GLAAD Media Award">GLAAD Media Awards</a> in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-jazz_jennings_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jazz_jennings-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-demi_lovato_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-demi_lovato-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Jenner's memoir, <i>The Secrets of My Life</i>, was published on April 25, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-Jenner2017_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jenner2017-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h2>
<p>Jenner is a <a href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christian</a>, leans towards political <a href="/wiki/Conservatism_in_the_United_States" title="Conservatism in the United States">conservatism</a>, and is a <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-christian_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-christian-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-republican_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-republican-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> "I have gotten more flak for being a conservative Republican than I have for being trans," she has said.<sup id="cite_ref-flak_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flak-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> Although stopping short of an endorsement, Jenner said she liked <a href="/wiki/Ted_Cruz" title="Ted Cruz">Ted Cruz</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_presidential_primaries,_2016" class="mw-redirect" title="Republican Party presidential primaries, 2016">2016 Republican presidential primaries</a>, despite Cruz's negative views of <a href="/wiki/Transgender" title="Transgender">trans people</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-i_like_ted_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-i_like_ted-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> On her reality show <i><a href="/wiki/I_Am_Cait" title="I Am Cait">I Am Cait</a></i>, Jenner said that although she does not support <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a>, she thinks he would be good for women's issues; she then stated she would never support <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-very_good_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-very_good-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> She ended up voting for Trump in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_elections,_2016" class="mw-redirect" title="United States presidential elections, 2016">2016 presidential election</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CNN_07262017_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN_07262017-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2017, President Trump rescinded federal requirements giving transgender students the <a href="/wiki/Transgender_rights_in_the_United_States#Schools" title="Transgender rights in the United States">right to choose the school restroom matching their gender identity</a>. In response, Jenner tweeted "Well @realDonaldTrump, from one Republican to another, this is a disaster. You made a promise to protect the LGBTQ community. Call me."<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2017, Jenner said she was in favor of <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_the_United_States" title="Same-sex marriage in the United States">same-sex marriage</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-gaytimesiam100behind_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gaytimesiam100behind-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2017, Jenner announced that she was contemplating running in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate_election_in_California,_2018" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Senate election in California, 2018">2018 race for the US Senate to represent California</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> Later in the month, she condemned Trump for issuing an order to reinstate a ban on transgender people from serving in the military. In her tweet, she wrote "What happened to your promise to fight for them?", juxtaposing it with Trump's tweet from June 2016 in which he promised to fight for the LGBT community.<sup id="cite_ref-CNN_07262017_188-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN_07262017-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In an October 2018 <i>Washington Post</i> opinion piece, she wrote that she was mistaken in her belief that Trump and his administration would support the LGBTQ community and vowed to learn from her error. "The reality is that the trans community is being relentlessly attacked by this president."<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> Her reversal came after a Trump administration proposal to restrict the legal definition of a person's gender to that assigned at birth.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marriages">Marriages</span></h3>
<p>Prior to her public gender transition, Jenner had been married three times, first to Chrystie Scott (<a href="/wiki/Given_name#Name_at_birth" title="Given name"><span title="Name at birth">n&#233;e</span></a> Crownover) from 1972 to 1981. They have two children, son Burton "Burt" Jenner and daughter Cassandra "Casey" Marino (<a href="/wiki/Given_name#Name_at_birth" title="Given name"><span title="Name at birth">n&#233;e</span></a> Jenner).<sup id="cite_ref-fantasy_man_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fantasy_man-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bwj_born_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bwj_born-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> Jenner and Scott's divorce was finalized the first week of January 1981.<sup id="cite_ref-wreckage_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wreckage-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On January 5, 1981, Jenner married actress <a href="/wiki/Linda_Thompson_(actress)" title="Linda Thompson (actress)">Linda Thompson</a> in Hawaii.<sup id="cite_ref-hee_haw_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hee_haw-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> They have two sons together, <a href="/wiki/Brandon_Jenner" class="mw-redirect" title="Brandon Jenner">Brandon Jenner</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brody_Jenner" title="Brody Jenner">Sam Brody Jenner</a> (known as Brody).<sup id="cite_ref-brody_joins_kuwtk_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brody_joins_kuwtk-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> By February 1986, Jenner and Thompson had separated and subsequently divorced.<sup id="cite_ref-happiness_not_working_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-happiness_not_working-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> Their sons later starred on the reality show <i><a href="/wiki/The_Princes_of_Malibu" title="The Princes of Malibu">The Princes of Malibu</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-follow_fox_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-follow_fox-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> and Brody appeared in the reality show <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hills_(TV_series)" title="The Hills (TV series)">The Hills</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-brody_slams_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brody_slams-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On April 21, 1991, Jenner married <a href="/wiki/Kris_Kardashian" class="mw-redirect" title="Kris Kardashian">Kris Kardashian</a> (<a href="/wiki/Given_name#Name_at_birth" title="Given name"><span title="Name at birth">n&#233;e</span></a> Houghton) after five months of dating.<sup id="cite_ref-j-k_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-j-k-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> They have two daughters, <a href="/wiki/Kendall_Jenner" title="Kendall Jenner">Kendall</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kylie_Jenner" title="Kylie Jenner">Kylie Jenner</a>. While married, Jenner was also the step-parent to Kris's children from her previous marriage&#160;&#8211;&#160;<a href="/wiki/Kourtney_Kardashian" title="Kourtney Kardashian">Kourtney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kim_Kardashian" title="Kim Kardashian">Kim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khlo%C3%A9_Kardashian" title="Khloé Kardashian">Khloé</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rob_Kardashian" title="Rob Kardashian">Robert</a>&#160;&#8211;&#160;who star in <i>Keeping Up with the Kardashians</i>. The couple announced their separation in October 2013,<sup id="cite_ref-much_happier_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-much_happier-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-always_love_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-always_love-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> though they had actually separated in June.<sup id="cite_ref-divorce_filings_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-divorce_filings-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> Kris filed for divorce in September 2014 citing <a href="/wiki/Irreconcilable_differences" title="Irreconcilable differences">irreconcilable differences</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11_months_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11_months-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> Their divorce terms were finalized in December 2014 and went into effect on March 23, 2015, because of a six-month state legal requirement.<sup id="cite_ref-divorce_finalized_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-divorce_finalized-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fatal_car_collision">Fatal car collision</span></h3>
<p>In February 2015, Jenner was involved in a fatal multiple-vehicle collision on the <a href="/wiki/California_State_Route_1" title="California State Route 1">Pacific Coast Highway</a> in <a href="/wiki/Malibu,_California" title="Malibu, California">Malibu, California</a>. Kim Howe, an <a href="/wiki/Animal_rights_activist" class="mw-redirect" title="Animal rights activist">animal rights activist</a> and actress, was killed when Jenner's <a href="/wiki/SUV" class="mw-redirect" title="SUV">SUV</a> ran into Howe's car. Accounts of the sequence of collisions have varied, as have the number of people injured.<sup id="cite_ref-6_refs_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6_refs-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> Prosecutors declined to file criminal charges, but three civil lawsuits were brought by Howe's stepchildren and drivers of other cars involved in the collision.<sup id="cite_ref-4_refs_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4_refs-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-KABC_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KABC-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> Jessica Steindorff, a Hollywood agent who was hit by Howe's car, settled her case in December 2015. Howe's stepchildren settled their case in January 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-settles_lawsuit_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-settles_lawsuit-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> Financial details were not disclosed in either case.<sup id="cite_ref-settles_fatal_crash_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-settles_fatal_crash-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
